# MCP Semantic Query (`db.semantic.query`)

This page documents the semantic-query engine under:

`com.github.salilvnair.convengine.engine.mcp.query.semantic`

It is the Text-to-AST-to-SQL runtime for ConvEngine MCP mode `semantic`.

<Highlight type="info" title="Core contract">
Semantic Query generates AST JSON with LLM, compiles SQL deterministically in Java, enforces policy guardrails, executes read-only SQL, and returns auditable result summaries.
</Highlight>

## Runtime request flow

  title="Semantic Query Runtime"
  subtitle="MCP planner -> semantic stages -> planner answer"

  edges={semanticQueryEdges}
  detailsById={semanticQueryDetails}
  defaultSelectedId="rts"
/>

## Libraries we use

Semantic Query runtime is built with a small set of focused libraries in `convengine/pom.xml`.

### Core dependencies (actual)

```xml
<dependency>
  <groupId>org.jooq</groupId>
  <artifactId>jooq</artifactId>
</dependency>

<dependency>
  <groupId>org.jgrapht</groupId>
  <artifactId>jgrapht-core</artifactId>
  <version>1.5.2</version>
</dependency>

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.fasterxml.jackson.dataformat</groupId>
  <artifactId>jackson-dataformat-yaml</artifactId>
</dependency>
```

<DbTable
  title="What each library is doing in semantic mode"
  columns={["Library", "Where used", "Role in runtime"]}
  rows={[
    ["jOOQ", "sql/handler/* + sql/compiler/*", "Builds SQL AST fragments and named-parameter SQL deterministically from canonical semantic AST."],
    ["JGraphT", "graph/provider/JGraphTSchemaGraphEngine", "Schema graph traversal + shortest join path resolution from FK metadata."],
    ["Jackson YAML", "model/SemanticModelLoader", "Loads semantic model (`semantic-layer.yaml`) into runtime model objects."]
  ]}
/>

## jOOQ in Semantic Query

jOOQ is not used as a codegen-first ORM here. It is used as a deterministic SQL construction layer controlled by the semantic compiler pipeline.

Flow:
1. LLM generates AST JSON.
2. AST is canonicalized and validated.
3. SQL handlers build clauses with jOOQ DSL + controlled SQL tokens.
4. SQL is emitted with named params.
5. JDBC executes with bind values.

### jOOQ conversion examples

<Tabs groupId="semantic-jooq-examples">
  <TabItem value="example1" label="Example 1: EQ + ILIKE" default>

```json
{
  "entity": "DisconnectRequest",
  "where": {
    "op": "AND",
    "conditions": [
      {"field": "requestStatus", "op": "EQ", "value": "FAILED"},
      {"field": "teamNotes", "op": "ILIKE", "value": "%inventory%"}
    ],
    "groups": []
  }
}
```

```java
// DefaultComparisonAstOperatorHandler
return DSL.condition("{0} " + sqlToken(operator) + " {1}", field, context.nextParam(value));
```

```sql
... WHERE ("t1"."request_status" = :p1 AND "t2"."zp_asr_team_notes" ILIKE :p2)
```

  </TabItem>
  <TabItem value="example2" label="Example 2: IN + BETWEEN + NULL checks">

```json
{
  "entity": "DisconnectRequest",
  "where": {
    "op": "AND",
    "conditions": [
      {"field": "accountId", "op": "IN", "value": ["UPSA100", "ACMA200"]},
      {"field": "requestedAt", "op": "BETWEEN", "value": ["2026-03-01T00:00:00Z", "2026-03-05T00:00:00Z"]},
      {"field": "disconnectId", "op": "IS_NULL", "value": null}
    ],
    "groups": []
  }
}
```

```java
// DefaultInAstOperatorHandler + DefaultBetweenAstOperatorHandler + DefaultNullCheckAstOperatorHandler
field.in(params)
DSL.condition("{0} BETWEEN {1} AND {2}", field, context.nextParam(v1), context.nextParam(v2))
field.isNull()
```

```sql
... WHERE ("t1"."account_id" IN (:p1, :p2)
       AND "t1"."requested_at" BETWEEN :p3 AND :p4
       AND "t0"."zp_disconnect_id" IS NULL)
```

  </TabItem>
  <TabItem value="example3" label="Example 3: ROW_NUMBER window">

```json
{
  "entity": "DisconnectRequest",
  "windows": [
    {
      "name": "account_rank",
      "function": "ROW_NUMBER",
      "partition_by": ["accountId"],
      "order_by": [{"field": "requestedAt", "direction": "DESC", "nulls": "LAST"}]
    }
  ]
}
```

```java
// DefaultRowNumberWindowFunctionHandler
return "ROW_NUMBER() OVER (" + overClause + ")";
```

```sql
ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY "t1"."account_id" ORDER BY "t1"."requested_at" DESC NULLS LAST) AS "account_rank"
```

  </TabItem>
</Tabs>

## JGraphT in Semantic Query

JGraphT powers schema traversal and shortest join-path resolution. It prevents LLM from inventing joins by computing paths from real FK metadata.

Flow:
1. Graph engine refreshes vertices/edges from schema inspector FK joins.
2. Join-path resolver chooses base table and initial required tables from retrieval.
3. SQL compile expands required tables from AST references (projections, `where`, `having`, `exists`, `subquery`, `sort`, `group_by`, `time_range`, metrics) before final join assembly.
4. Shortest paths are found with hop limits.
5. Resolved edges are de-duplicated and returned to compiler.

### JGraphT traversal examples

<Tabs groupId="semantic-jgrapht-examples">
  <TabItem value="graph1" label="Example 1: Graph build" default>

```java
// JGraphTSchemaGraphEngine.refreshGraph()
for (Map<String, Object> row : joins) {
  String sourceTable = text(row.get("source_table"));
  String targetTable = text(row.get("target_table"));
  nextGraph.addVertex(sourceTable);
  nextGraph.addVertex(targetTable);
  nextGraph.addEdge(sourceTable, targetTable);
  nextGraph.addEdge(targetTable, sourceTable); // reverse edge
}
```

```text
Result: directed graph with forward + reverse FK edges for traversal flexibility.
```

  </TabItem>
  <TabItem value="graph2" label="Example 2: Shortest path">

```java
// JGraphTSchemaGraphEngine.shortestPath()
while (!queue.isEmpty()) {
  NodePath current = queue.poll();
  if (current.node().equals(toTable)) {
    return toEdges(current.path());
  }
  for (String next : neighbors(current.node())) {
    if (!visited.contains(next)) {
      queue.add(new NodePath(next, nextPath));
      visited.add(next);
    }
  }
}
```

```text
Uses BFS-style traversal; returns concrete SchemaEdge list for SQL joins.
```

  </TabItem>
  <TabItem value="graph3" label="Example 3: Resolve plan">

```java
// DefaultJoinPathResolver.doResolve()
String base = candidates.get(0).name();
for (String target : requiredTables) {
  List<SchemaEdge> path = graph.shortestPath(base, target, maxHops);
  if (path == null || path.isEmpty()) unresolved.add(target);
  else merge(path);
}
return new JoinPathPlan(base, merged, requiredTables, unresolved, confidence);
```

```text
Compiler receives resolved edges and unresolved table list; validator blocks unresolved joins.
```

  </TabItem>
</Tabs>

## AST model capabilities

### Operators in AST model

`AstOperator.java` includes:
- `ILIKE`
- `BETWEEN`
- `IN`
- `NOT_IN`
- `IS_NULL`
- `IS_NOT_NULL`

Normalization behavior in `AstFilter`/`AstSubqueryFilter` also accepts aggregate-style tokens and maps to base operators:
- `COUNT_GT` -> `GT`
- `SUM_GTE` -> `GTE`
- `COUNT_NOT_IN` -> `NOT_IN`
- `*_NOTNULL` -> `IS_NOT_NULL`

### New AST nodes

- Boolean tree: `AstFilterGroup.java`
- Exists: `AstExistsBlock.java`
- Subquery filters: `AstSubqueryFilter.java`, `AstSubquerySpec.java`
- Windows: `AstWindowSpec.java`
- Full v1 payload: `SemanticQueryAstV1.java`

### Correlated field reference rule

For `exists.where` and `subquery_filters.where`, a value starting with `$` is treated as an outer-field reference, not a string literal.

- `$disconnectId` means "compare against outer query field `disconnectId`"
- Resolver maps that field using outer entity semantic field mapping + outer aliases

Example AST:

```json
{
  "exists": [
    {
      "entity": "DisconnectRequest",
      "where": {
        "op": "AND",
        "conditions": [
          { "field": "disconnectId", "op": "=", "value": "$disconnectId" }
        ],
        "groups": []
      },
      "not_exists": false
    }
  ]
}
```

Compiled SQL shape:

```sql
EXISTS (
  SELECT 1
  FROM zp_request ex1
  LEFT JOIN zp_disconnect_order exj2 ON ex1.zp_request_id = exj2.zp_request_id
  WHERE exj2.zp_disconnect_id = t0.zp_disconnect_id
)
```

### Validation coverage

`DefaultAstValidator.java` validates:
- entity and field existence
- operator and value compatibility (`ILIKE` string-only, `BETWEEN` two values, `IN`/`NOT_IN` array)
- exists blocks
- subquery filters
- window specs
- groupBy/metric constraints

### SQL rendering coverage

- <span className="ce-semantic-op">LIKE</span>/<span className="ce-semantic-op">comparison</span>: <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultComparisonAstOperatorHandler.java</span>
- <span className="ce-semantic-op">BETWEEN</span>: <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultBetweenAstOperatorHandler.java</span>
- <span className="ce-semantic-op">IN</span>/<span className="ce-semantic-op">NOT_IN</span>: <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultInAstOperatorHandler.java</span>
- <span className="ce-semantic-op">IS_NULL</span>/<span className="ce-semantic-op">IS_NOT_NULL</span>: <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultNullCheckAstOperatorHandler.java</span>
- <span className="ce-semantic-op">ROW_NUMBER</span> window: <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultRowNumberWindowFunctionHandler.java</span>

### <span className="ce-semantic-accent">DATE_TRUNC status</span>

Not active yet:
- Placeholder exists in <span className="ce-semantic-chip">DefaultFunctionClauseHandler.java</span>
- Missing concrete AST field + validator + function handler for <span className="ce-semantic-accent">DATE_TRUNC</span>

### Static DB rows required
